CC   -!- FUNCTION: Acts as component of the CYC8-TUP1 corepressor complex
CC       which is involved in the repression of many genes in a wide
CC       variety of physiological processes including heme-regulated and
CC       catabolite repressed genes. May also be involved in the
CC       derepression of at least some target genes. The complex is
CC       recruited to target genes by interaction with DNA-bound
CC       transcriptional repressors, like MATALPHA2, MIG1, RFX1 and SKO1.
CC       The complex recruits histone deacetylases to produce a repressive
CC       chromatin structure, interacts with hypoacetylated N-terminal
CC       tails of histones H3 and H4 that have been programmed for
CC       repression by the action of histone deacetylases and interferes
CC       directly with the transcriptional machinery by associating with
CC       the RNA polymerase II mediator complex.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10722672, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11069890,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11230135, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11784848,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14665463}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Associates with TUP1 to form the CYC8-TUP1 (or TUP1-SSN6)
CC       corepressor complex that is composed of 4 copies of TUP1 and one
CC       copy of CYC8. Interacts with MATALPHA2, CTI6, MIG1, TUP1, SUT1,
CC       RFX1, PGD1, HOS1, HOS2 AND RPD3. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10722672,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10759558, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11069890,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11401714, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12086626,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14525981, ECO:0000269|PubMed:7498787,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:7724528, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8943325,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9741624}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P53096:HOS2; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-18215, EBI-8475;
CC       P40356:PGD1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-18215, EBI-13268;
CC       P48743:RFX1; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-18215, EBI-15036;
CC       P32561:RPD3; NbExp=6; IntAct=EBI-18215, EBI-15864;
CC       P16649:TUP1; NbExp=5; IntAct=EBI-18215, EBI-19654;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Nucleus.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The prion domain (PrD) is a Gln/Asn (Q/N)-rich domain,
CC       which is unstructured in its native, soluble form, and which forms
CC       a parallel in-register beta-sheet in its amyloid form.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: [OCT+] is the prion form of CYC8. [OCT+] is the
CC       result of a conformational change of the cellular CYC8 protein
CC       that becomes self-propagating and infectious. [OCT+]-aggregates
CC       sequester soluble CYC8, resulting in increased levels of iso-2-
CC       cytochrome c, defects in sporulation and mating, higher levels of
CC       invertase derepression and increased flocculation, reminiscent of
CC       a partial loss of function of the CYC8-TUP1 corepressor complex.
CC       [OCT+] can be cured by GdnHCl and by inactivation of the molecular
CC       chaperone HSP104, which is required for [OCT+] propagation. It is
CC       speculated that prion properties of transcription factors may
CC       generate an optimized phenotypic heterogeneity that buffers yeast
CC       populations against diverse environmental insults.
CC       {ECO:0000305|PubMed:19219034}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 3890 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the CYC8/SSN6 family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 10 TPR repeats. {ECO:0000255|PROSITE-
CC       ProRule:PRU00339}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Has a role in both calcium and manganese homeostasis.
CC       Involved in the transfer of iron and Mn(2+) from the cytosol to
CC       the vacuole for storage of these metals.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11390404, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8668190,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8866476}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P36156:ECM4; NbExp=1; IntAct=EBI-2048372, EBI-2042717;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Golgi apparatus membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11390404, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562095,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8866476}. Vacuole membrane {ECO:0000305};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Down-regulated under iron starvation by TIS11.
CC       Transcriptionally up-regulated by YAP5 in response to increased
CC       cytosolic iron. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15652485,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18070921}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Deletion causes an increase in metal
CC       sensitivity at 15 mM manganese, but does not affect invertase
CC       glycosylation. Deletion shows increased sensitivity to external
CC       iron, which is suppressed by MRS3 or MRS4 overexpression requiring
CC       oxygen but not respiration, and exacerbated by ectopic expression
CC       of the iron transporter FET4. Deletion also results in decreased
CC       vacuolar iron content and decreased iron stores, which affect
CC       cytosolic iron levels and cell growth. Deletion together with MRS3
CC       and MRS4 restores cellular and mitochondrial iron homeostasis to
CC       near normal level, corrects the MRS3 and MRS4 double deletion
CC       phenotype (which shows increased resistance to cobalt but
CC       decreased resistance to copper and cadmium), and has near normal
CC       levels of aconitase activity. When overexpressed, maintains
CC       respiratory function in a YFH1 deletion mutant regardless of
CC       extracellular iron concentration, activates the iron-dependent
CC       transcription factor AFT1 resulting in an increase in iron uptake,
CC       cytosolic iron accumulation and a change in copper metabolism.
CC       Overexpression prevents excessive mitochondrial iron accumulation
CC       by limiting mitochondrial iron uptake and results in increased
CC       expression of the high affinity iron transport system composed of
CC       FET3 and FTR1. Overexpression also suppresses the rapamycin-
CC       resistant phenotype of PMR1 deletion mutant.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8866476}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 2840 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the CCC1 family. {ECO:0000305}.

RT   "A lack of Birbeck granules in Langerhans cells is associated with a
RT   naturally occurring point mutation in the human Langerin gene.";
RL   J. Invest. Dermatol. 124:714-717(2005).
RN   [12]
RP   VARIANTS ALA-278; ASP-288 AND PRO-300, CHARACTERIZATION OF VARIANT
RP   BIRGD ARG-264, AND CHARACTERIZATION OF VARIANTS ALA-278; ASP-288 AND
RP   PRO-300.
RX   PubMed=16567809; DOI=10.1074/jbc.M511502200;
RA   Ward E.M., Stambach N.S., Drickamer K., Taylor M.E.;
RT   "Polymorphisms in human langerin affect stability and sugar binding
RT   activity.";
RL   J. Biol. Chem. 281:15450-15456(2006).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Calcium-dependent lectin displaying mannose-binding
CC       specificity. Induces the formation of Birbeck granules (BGs); is a
CC       potent regulator of membrane superimposition and zippering. Binds
CC       to sulfated as well as mannosylated glycans, keratan sulfate (KS)
CC       and beta-glucans. Facilitates uptake of antigens and is involved
CC       in the routing and/or processing of antigen for presentation to T
CC       cells. Major receptor on primary Langerhans cells for Candida
CC       species, Saccharomyces species, and Malassezia furfur. Protects
CC       against human immunodeficiency virus-1 (HIV-1) infection. Binds to
CC       high-mannose structures present on the envelope glycoprotein which
CC       is followed by subsequent targeting of the virus to the Birbeck
CC       granules leading to its rapid degradation.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10661407, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17334373,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20026605, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20097424}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homotrimer. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12626394}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10661407};
CC       Single-pass type II membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10661407}. Note=Found in Birbeck granules
CC       (BGs), which are organelles consisting of superimposed and
CC       zippered membranes.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Exclusively expressed by Langerhans cells.
CC       Expressed in astrocytoma and malignant ependymoma, but not in
CC       normal brain tissues. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10661407,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20026605}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The C-type lectin domain mediates dual recognition of both
CC       sulfated and mannosylated glycans. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:20026605}.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Birbeck granule deficiency (BIRGD) [MIM:613393]: A
CC       condition characterized by the absence of Birbeck granules in
CC       epidermal Langerhans cells. Despite the lack of Birbeck granules,
CC       Langerhans cells are present in normal numbers and have normal
CC       morphologic characteristics and antigen-presenting capacity.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15816828}. Note=The disease is caused by
CC       mutations affecting the gene represented in this entry.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 C-type lectin domain. {ECO:0000255|PROSITE-
CC       ProRule:PRU00040}.

CC       Note=Langerin;
CC       URL="http://www.functionalglycomics.org/glycomics/GBPServlet?&operationType=view&cbpId=cbp_hum_Ctlect_00126";

RA   Starita L.M., Lo R.S., Eng J.K., von Haller P.D., Fields S.;
RT   "Sites of ubiquitin attachment in Saccharomyces cerevisiae.";
RL   Proteomics 12:236-240(2012).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Required for the sorting and concentration of proteins
CC       resulting in the entry of these proteins into the invaginating
CC       vesicles of the multivesicular body (MVB). Acts a component of the
CC       ESCRT-III complex, which appears to be critical for late steps in
CC       MVB sorting, such as membrane invagination and final cargo sorting
CC       and recruitment of late-acting components of the sorting
CC       machinery. The MVB pathway requires the sequential function of
CC       ESCRT-O, -I,-II and -III complex assemblies. Appears to sequester
CC       MVB cargo. Recruits BRO1, which in turn recruits DOA4, which
CC       deubiquitinates cargos before their enclosure within MVB vesicles.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11559748, ECO:0000269|PubMed:12194857}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Self-associates. Core component of the ESCRT-III complex
CC       (endosomal sorting required for transport complex III). ESCRT-III
CC       appears to be sequentially assembled as a flat lattice on the
CC       endosome membrane and forms a transient 450 kDa complex that
CC       contains DID4, oligomerized SNF7, VPS20 and VPS24. SNF7
CC       oligomerization into a membrane-associated filament is nucleated
CC       by association of SNF7 with VPS20; the process is terminated
CC       through association of VPS24, possibly by capping the SNF7
CC       filament. VPS24 subsequently associates with DID4/VPS2. Interacts
CC       with VTA1; the interaction requires DID2. Interacts with BRO1.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12194857, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15086794,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15935782, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16601096}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Self; NbExp=7; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-17554;
CC       P48582:BRO1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-3768;
CC       P36108:DID4; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-26574;
CC       Q03281:HEH2; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-22131;
CC       Q04272:VPS20; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-28157;
CC       P52917:VPS4; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-17554, EBI-20475;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12194857}.
CC       Endosome membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12194857}; Peripheral
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12194857}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Present with 3270 molecules/cell in log phase SD
CC       medium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14562106}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the SNF7 family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Was originally thought to be a nuclear protein and
CC       mutations were shown to prevent full derepression of the SUC2
CC       (invertase) gene. {ECO:0000305|PubMed:8224817}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Pre-vacuolar protein sorting protein involved in the
CC       transport of biosynthetic membrane proteins from the
CC       prevacuolar/endosomal compartment to the vacuole. Required for
CC       multivesicular body (MVB) protein sorting. Catalyzes the ATP-
CC       dependent dissociation of class E VPS proteins from endosomal
CC       membranes, such as the disassembly of the ESCRT-III complex.
CC       Required for extracellular secretion of the secreted aspartyl
CC       proteases SAP2, SAP4, SAP5, and SAP6. Its regulation of the pre-
CC       vacuolar secretory pathway is critical for virulence.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15590834, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17506830,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:18814053, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19819358,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20026677, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20581294,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22427429, ECO:0000269|PubMed:25483774}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer or homodimer (in nucleotide-free form). Decamer,
CC       dodecamer or tetradecamer of two stacked respective homooligomeric
CC       rings (when bound to ATP); the dodecameric form seems to be
CC       predominant. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P52917}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Endosome membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P52917}; Peripheral membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Expression is regulated by GCN2 and GCN4.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16215176}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Leads to defects in endocytosis. Displays a
CC       characteristic class E vacuolar morphology and multilamellar
CC       structures consistent with an aberrant prevacuolar compartment.
CC       Missorts several vacuolar proteins to the extracellular space,
CC       including carboxypeptidase (CPY), vacuolar protease A (PrA), and
CC       vacuolar protease B (PrB). In addition, certain soluble secretory
CC       proteins, such as invertase and acid phosphatase, are missorted
CC       from the pre-vacuolar compartment (PVC) to the general secretory
CC       pathway prior to exocytosis. Results also in a decrease of
CC       canonically secreted proteins. Shows increased biofilm formation.
CC       Causes reduced tissue damage in an in vitro oral epithelial model
CC       (OEM) of tissue invasion, and defects in macrophage killing in
CC       vitro. Shows also attenuated virulence in an in vivo

RT   "Production of high concentrations of ethanol from inulin by

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Endo-inulinase involved in utilization of the plant
CC       storage polymer inulin, consisting of fructooligosaccharides with
CC       a degree of polymerization (DP) value from 2 to 60.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (2->1)-beta-D-fructosidic
CC       linkages in inulin. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402}.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Activity is stimulated by Mn(2+), Fe(2+) Ca(2+)
CC       metal ions and DTT; and inhibited by glucose, Mg(2+), Zn(2+),
CC       Cu(2+), Hg(2+), Al(3+), and Fe(3+). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402}.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=2.57 mM for inulin {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402};
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 4.5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402};
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 55 degrees Celsius.
CC         {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15135402};
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- BIOTECHNOLOGY: Plays an important role in biofuel production. Pure
CC       nonhydrolyzed inulin can be directly converted to ethanol in a
CC       simultaneous saccharification and fermentation process when
CC       combining A.niger and S.cerevisiae. Endoinulinase can digest
CC       fructooligosaccharides with high degree of polymerization (DP)
CC       values (>20) into short molecules that may be readily hydrolyzed
CC       by S.cerevisiae SUC2. Thus, introduction of an endoinulinase gene
CC       into S.cerevisiae will improve its inulin utilization and ethanol
CC       fermentation through collaboration between the heterologous
CC       endoinulinase and the invertase SUC2.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8481000}.

CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RT   "Improved ethanol fermentation by heterologous endoinulinase and
RT   inherent invertase from inulin by Saccharomyces cerevisiae.";

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Endo-inulinase involved in utilization of the plant
CC       storage polymer inulin, consisting of fructooligosaccharides with
CC       a degree of polymerization (DP) value from 2 to 60.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23683966}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (2->1)-beta-D-fructosidic
CC       linkages in inulin. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23683966}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Expression is induced in presence of sucrose or inulin
CC       and controlled by the catabolite repressor creA and by the
CC       inulinolytic genes regulator inuR. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17005986,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17917744}.
CC   -!- BIOTECHNOLOGY: Plays an important role in biofuel production. Pure
CC       nonhydrolyzed inulin can be directly converted to ethanol in a
CC       simultaneous saccharification and fermentation process when
CC       combining A.niger and S.cerevisiae. Endoinulinase can digest
CC       fructooligosaccharides with high degree of polymerization (DP)
CC       values (>20) into short molecules that may be readily hydrolyzed
CC       by S.cerevisiae SUC2. Thus, introduction of an endoinulinase gene
CC       into S.cerevisiae will improve its inulin utilization and ethanol
CC       fermentation through collaboration between the heterologous
CC       endoinulinase and the invertase SUC2.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23683966, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8481000}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 32 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Strain CBS 513.88 / FGSC A1513 contains only one gene
CC       encoding for an extracellular endo-inulinase (inuA), contrary to
CC       other strains containing two genes (inuA and inuB). {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Endo-inulinase involved in utilization of the plant
CC       storage polymer inulin, consisting of fructooligosaccharides with
CC       a degree of polymerization (DP) value from 2 to 60. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (2->1)-beta-D-fructosidic
CC       linkages in inulin.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- BIOTECHNOLOGY: Plays an important role in biofuel production. Pure
CC       nonhydrolyzed inulin can be directly converted to ethanol in a
CC       simultaneous saccharification and fermentation process when
CC       combining A.niger and S.cerevisiae. Endoinulinase can digest
CC       fructooligosaccharides with high degree of polymerization (DP)
CC       values (>20) into short molecules that may be readily hydrolyzed
CC       by S.cerevisiae SUC2. Thus, introduction of an endoinulinase gene
CC       into S.cerevisiae will improve its inulin utilization and ethanol
CC       fermentation through collaboration between the heterologous
CC       endoinulinase and the invertase SUC2.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8481000}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 32 family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.
